    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<span id="freeTextContainer15442931019999038146">It's almost Christmas. Cecilia lies sick in bed as her family bustle around her to make her last Christmas as special as possible. Cecilia has cancer.   <span id="freeText15442931019999038146" style="display:none">It's almost Christmas. Cecilia lies sick in bed as her family bustle around her to make her last Christmas as special as possible. Cecilia has cancer. An angel steps through her window. So begins a spirited and engaging series of conversations between Cecelia and her angel. As the sick girl thinks about her life and prepares for her death, she changes subtly, in herself and in her relationships with her family. Jostein Gaarder is a profoundly optimistic writer, who writes about death with wisdom, compassion and an enquiring mind. 'Through a Glass, Darkly' will not only bring comfort to the bereaved. It will move and amaze everyone who reads it.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer205333453" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10942657070323914214">So there's an angel and a sick girl who discuss heaven, creation and earth while sneaking out into winter nights ... if you haven't read Jostein Gaarder before that must've seemed pretty strange. Also, if you haven't read Jostein Gaarder before you're missing out on something wonderful. As with all of his books he writes children like he is one. There's a beautiful innocence and curiosity about his protagonists that you can easily get carried away with. He's also very fond of philosophy but in t</span>
  <span id="freeText10942657070323914214" style="display:none">So there's an angel and a sick girl who discuss heaven, creation and earth while sneaking out into winter nights ... if you haven't read Jostein Gaarder before that must've seemed pretty strange. Also, if you haven't read Jostein Gaarder before you're missing out on something wonderful. As with all of his books he writes children like he is one. There's a beautiful innocence and curiosity about his protagonists that you can easily get carried away with. He's also very fond of philosophy but in this book, unlike Sophie's World, he explores it more as a matter of circumstance rather than lecturing. This book is sweet, sad, funny and beautiful. It's why people read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10942657070323914214" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer40952779" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3407248533767922382">A sweet story with beautiful thoughts and ideas, but one that is executed in a way that is just not to my taste. I've never cared for novels that are really a dialogue between two individuals to get across the author's philosophy or viewpoint. Perhaps I'd have felt differently if I could've read this when I was young.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_130254247" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/130254247" />
    <a title="Saravannan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4527755-saravannan"><img alt="Saravannan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1550369424p2/4527755.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/130254247?book_show_action=true">Nov 11, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Saravannan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Saravannan" href="/user/show/4527755-saravannan">Saravannan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780753806739" href="/book/show/175831.Through_A_Glass_Darkly">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527755-saravannan?shelf=philosophical">philosophical</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer130254247" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10358585526280211110">I was not halfway thru the book when I knew I would not like it and I was quite right. I was quite disappointed with the book. It has no plot what so ever. It has 2 individual talking about life, heaven, God, and things like that. I think this book is meant to make us think, provoke our thoughts, and make us wonder. And quite honestly, it didn’t. In fact, I think some of the statements contradict with each other. <br/><br/>For example, Ariel states that God was very tired after the 7th day (after creating</span>
  <span id="freeText10358585526280211110" style="display:none">I was not halfway thru the book when I knew I would not like it and I was quite right. I was quite disappointed with the book. It has no plot what so ever. It has 2 individual talking about life, heaven, God, and things like that. I think this book is meant to make us think, provoke our thoughts, and make us wonder. And quite honestly, it didn’t. In fact, I think some of the statements contradict with each other. <br /><br />For example, Ariel states that God was very tired after the 7th day (after creating the world of course), but few pages after that, he talks about fishes evolving into amphibians and start walking on land (which suggests evolution theory is correct, i.e. the world and animals took billions of years to be created as it is now). <br /><br />Another example is Ariel said that since he is not made of flesh and blood, he can’t ‘feel’ anything, but later in the book, he claimed that he has a lot of fun jumping across asteroids and riding comets. He also laughs at certain points in the book. How can he know what is ‘fun’ and ‘funny’ when he can’t ‘feel’ anything?<br /><br />Anyway, even though being a short story as it is (only 161 pages), I really struggled to finish it. I even skipped few pages to go straight to the ending. And it still made no difference, I still didn’t like the book.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10358585526280211110" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13249150-binibining-e-of-the-ugly-writers?shelf=four-enjoyable-stars">four-enjoyable-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13249150-binibining-e-of-the-ugly-writers?shelf=i-own-these">i-own-these</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13249150-binibining-e-of-the-ugly-writers?shelf=my-2016-reads">my-2016-reads</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer680123016" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4951297796365344001"><b>
  <i>"Did you know that something can be so nice it almost hurts?"</i>
</b><br/><br/><b>
  <i>Because you can't run away from your own souls. You can't bite your own tails. Or perhaps that's exactly what you do: you bite your own tails until you shout and scream in fear and terror.</i>
</b><br/><br/>The story was about the everyday conversation between an Angel and a sick little girl. This was very touching, very soulful and beautiful. It touched me and was in awe. <br/><br/>It kind of made me sad in the end though. It was all about life, death and</span>
  <span id="freeText4951297796365344001" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>"Did you know that something can be so nice it almost hurts?"</i>
</b><br /><br /><b>
  <i>Because you can't run away from your own souls. You can't bite your own tails. Or perhaps that's exactly what you do: you bite your own tails until you shout and scream in fear and terror.</i>
</b><br /><br />The story was about the everyday conversation between an Angel and a sick little girl. This was very touching, very soulful and beautiful. It touched me and was in awe. <br /><br />It kind of made me sad in the end though. It was all about life, death and acceptance. The little girl was all over the place her feelings about everything i mean from anger, sadness, i think a bit of depression and eventually acceptance. I like the Angel he was so cool and very talkative for an Angel of Death that is. It was an easy read and unique since it tackles different topics also. From the creation, Adam and Eve to science and astronomy and angels to how humans feel from physical to emotional. This book is interesting. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>"We see everything in a glass, darkly. Sometimes we can peer through the glass and catch a glimpse of what is on the other side. If we were to polish the glass clean we'd see much more. But then we would no longer see ourselves."</i>
</b><br /><br />Jostein Gaarder was a very good author indeed. The way he depicted the angels and God was very cool. I cant wait to read more of his works. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4951297796365344001" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780753806739" href="/book/show/175831.Through_A_Glass_Darkly">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1215302-nancy?shelf=still-owned">still-owned</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer904743347" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18344402859891102796">As Cecelia lies dying of a form of childhood cancer, she is visted by the Angel Ariel. Together they discuss what it means to be human, what it means to have a soul and how humans and angels differ. This is a sweet and sad book, although it is a bit too religious for my tastes. It didn't really come close to Sophie's World.</span>

          </span>

    <a title="Nina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4693968-nina"><img alt="Nina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1402362021p2/4693968.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/290552804?book_show_action=true">Mar 07, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nina" href="/user/show/4693968-nina">Nina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4693968-nina?shelf=non-fantasy">non-fantasy</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4693968-nina?shelf=stand-alone">stand-alone</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4693968-nina?shelf=a-1-star">a-1-star</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer290552804" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10756139857788056704">Can you blame me if I want something less, well, divine from this story? It is Josten Gaarder's first book I've ever read, and I don't feel like reading her other book. It was a good read, but I was bored and I wasn't feeling anything when I read this.<br/><br/>What helps me through is my curiosity to Cecilia and Ariel's ending. But then again, the whole book made me think some stupid questions like, "hell, what in the world is Cecilia thinking?" or "what is she doing?" or worse, "why is she such a grim g</span>
  <span id="freeText10756139857788056704" style="display:none">Can you blame me if I want something less, well, divine from this story? It is Josten Gaarder's first book I've ever read, and I don't feel like reading her other book. It was a good read, but I was bored and I wasn't feeling anything when I read this.<br /><br />What helps me through is my curiosity to Cecilia and Ariel's ending. But then again, the whole book made me think some stupid questions like, "hell, what in the world is Cecilia thinking?" or "what is she doing?" or worse, "why is she such a grim girl with no joy in her heart?". I mean, come on, for a little girl she's pretty pessimistic. She's so bitter, seeing the world with gray, and half of through the story I was tired with her attitude to Ariel, her stupidity and naivety, her bitter remarks for everything. I feel like slapping her in the face and tell her to just shut up and listen to what Ariel says without she commenting. Ugh. <br />Ariel is not my usual kind of angel. It was disappointing. At first, I wanted an image like Raphael the Archangel, or Patch Cipriano, hell, or even Aaron Corbett. Something with wings, maybe. But Ariel is not!<br /><br />And the issue, about God and questions about God, well, I'm not very fond of it. Just let say I particularly dislike this story. I'm no a conservative, but what they're questioning about was a little disturbing, and even right now I can't remember what they're talking about!<br /><br />Honestly, I hate to give a book one star, but what choice do I have? I don't like the story, I don't like the characters, I hate the way it ends, so I'm sorry for Miss Gaarder's fans, I can't wrap my head around it and I decided to give the book back to its previous owner soon, as I don't know what to do with a book I don't intend to re-read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10756139857788056704" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer725719301" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6294301555760383771">Before I started reading this book, I knew I could expect lots and lots of philosophic thoughts in a book by Jostein Gaarder. I knew it would make me think about things I will never understand and maybe even don't want to understand. Nevertheless I started reading this little book "Through a glass, darkly".<br/><br/>Though the story is a little dark and sad, there are some deep thoughts in it. Most of these thought are really Christian ideas about heaven and God. I believe that non-Christian people won't </span>
  <span id="freeText6294301555760383771" style="display:none">Before I started reading this book, I knew I could expect lots and lots of philosophic thoughts in a book by Jostein Gaarder. I knew it would make me think about things I will never understand and maybe even don't want to understand. Nevertheless I started reading this little book "Through a glass, darkly".<br /><br />Though the story is a little dark and sad, there are some deep thoughts in it. Most of these thought are really Christian ideas about heaven and God. I believe that non-Christian people won't like this book at all because God is omnipresent in it. <br />I'm not sure I liked the book. It certainly made me think about some things but the "big" problem is I don't know what to think about afterlife and heaven and that's what the book keeps talking about.<br /><br />In this story we meet Cecelia, a girl who's terminally ill. She can only lay in her bed and is too sick to celebrate Christmas, her favorite time of the year. While Cecelia is in bed and dreams about trees, presents and Christmasfood, she meets the angel Ariel. Ariel is a funny angel whose presence is appreciated a lot by Cecelia. She likes talking to him about heaven and he likes to learn new things about people. Cecelia wants to know how it is to be an angel, to float, to know God,... and Ariel can't wait to hear how it feels when you're made of flesh and blood, dream, feel pain,...Towards the end of Cecelia's life, Ariel visits her more and more so when Cecelia leaves the world her family and friends live in, she's already used to some things in heaven and isn't afraid of it anymore...<br /><br />Not bad, but not entirely my thing too...</span>
  <a data-text-id="6294301555760383771" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13233768166511202959">"Did you know that something can be so nice it almost hurts?" <br/>Because you can't run away from your own souls. You can't bite your own tails.   <span id="freeText13233768166511202959" style="display:none">"Did you know that something can be so nice it almost hurts?" <br />Because you can't run away from your own souls. You can't bite your own tails. Or perhaps that's exactly what you do: you bite your own tails until you shout and scream in fear and terror.<br /><br />"Flesh and blood are no more than earth and water, after all. But God has breathed some of his spirit into you. That is why there is a part of you that is God"..<br /><br /> The book has aroused that inescapable feeling of being lost in my ignorance.<br />I felt like WHAT ARE YOU TRYING TO SAY?? <br />Gaarder has a singular way of thinking, he's a master in stimulating curiosity, I admire his sense of seeing standards in a different way and giving them new metaphors.<br /> I will never reach the glory of conceiving his notions, there will be always between and behind the lines..<br />This time he's asking about angels, what would it be like to be an angel? what would it be like to live out of the muddy thing you live within or with, or through..<br />Would you choose to live in an angelic realm? Would it be intriguing to get red of that muddy mold that chains you to sorrows, sickness, fragility, sadness yet, hope, love, faith, tranquility…? <br /></span>

<div id="review_486627263" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/486627263" />
    <a title="luscious" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11345471-luscious"><img alt="luscious" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1343853451p2/11345471.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/486627263?book_show_action=true">Dec 27, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="luscious" class="user" itemprop="url" name="luscious" href="/user/show/11345471-luscious">luscious</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11345471-luscious?shelf=luscious-bookshelf">luscious-bookshelf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer486627263" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5602323763039738952">Since I lost my mother last year, I've been more or less on the prowl for novels that chronicle loss and the experience of letting someone go. However, I'm more interested in how the person who is actually forced to leave this world experiences all this as I watched my mom go through it all.<br/><br/>Jostein Gaarder succeeded in establishing the realm in which Cecilia finds herself as she is facing the inevitable. I really liked the shifts we can see her go into, all the while she's uttering things that m</span>
  <span id="freeText5602323763039738952" style="display:none">Since I lost my mother last year, I've been more or less on the prowl for novels that chronicle loss and the experience of letting someone go. However, I'm more interested in how the person who is actually forced to leave this world experiences all this as I watched my mom go through it all.<br /><br />Jostein Gaarder succeeded in establishing the realm in which Cecilia finds herself as she is facing the inevitable. I really liked the shifts we can see her go into, all the while she's uttering things that make you consider your everyday life...<br />The author uses the apparition of an 'angel', Ariel, to get Cecilia to come to terms with her fate. While this is not bad (it is most probably a figment of her mind), one has to keep up with the many references to God, as the family is religious. Being a non-believer myself, I had to turn the switch quite a few times. <br /><br />Overall, nice young adult novel.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5602323763039738952" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_801607679" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/801607679" />
    <a title="Sandra" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1478030-sandra"><img alt="Sandra" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1574023546p2/1478030.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/801607679?book_show_action=true">Dec 27, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sandra" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sandra" href="/user/show/1478030-sandra">Sandra</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9783446180710" href="/book/show/1212517.Durch_einen_Spiegel_in_einem_dunklen_Wort">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1478030-sandra?shelf=e-books">e-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1478030-sandra?shelf=in-german">in-german</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1478030-sandra?shelf=read-in-2013">read-in-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1478030-sandra?shelf=norse-mythology">norse-mythology</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer801607679" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11739049829231238101">I picked up this book because I thought the title was very interesting. I was happily surprised that it had a sort of Christmas theme in it. It fits with the time of year, after all! <br/><br/>Another thing that surprised me was that this wasn't an easy book to read at all. I had thought this to be a book for kids or young adults, but I've read literary articles that were easier to read than this book. I think that's just personal preference however: most of this book, at least the most important part of </span>
  <span id="freeText11739049829231238101" style="display:none">I picked up this book because I thought the title was very interesting. I was happily surprised that it had a sort of Christmas theme in it. It fits with the time of year, after all! <br /><br />Another thing that surprised me was that this wasn't an easy book to read at all. I had thought this to be a book for kids or young adults, but I've read literary articles that were easier to read than this book. I think that's just personal preference however: most of this book, at least the most important part of it, is a philosophical conversation between human Cecilie and angel Ariel. This format didn't just make the book a bit hard to read, it also illuminated very clearly that an actual plot was not the most important thing for the writer. For instance, Cecilie is very ill, and we do see glimpses of that, but never enough to make a real lasting impression. Characterization and plot are both not really expanded upon, to make way for the religious philosophy that's at the heart of the book.<br /><br />Truthfully, I liked the philosophical thoughts portrayed in this book. Gaarder does a good job of mixing Bible references, Norse mythology references, as well as science (astronomy and evolution, mostly) into a comprehendable world-view. But, for me there were quite a few inconsistencies in the mythology:<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[- Angels aren't supposed to sense or feel things. This means that flying doens't bring them joy, touching snow doesn't make them feel the cold, etc. Ariel stresses very often that angels don't feel anything. But somehow they do feel the need to be alone every once in a while (as illustrated by the fact that Ariel sometimes goes to an asteroid I think it was because (s)he doesn't want to see anyone for a while). Also kind of strange: Ariel says they know everything they need to know. He can't forget or remember anything: every knowledge they need is present. But still they feel curious about how it is to be human. This is strange again: because curiosity is an emotion. I don't know, for me this seems inconsistent. <br /><br />- God is portrayed as omniscient. But still, he didn't know how his creation would turn out, as he has no control over what he created. Maybe it's my interpretation of the word omniscient that's the problem here, but I think that shows God does not know everything. But then, how to draw the line? Odin for instance is not portrayed as omniscient, but he's said to have become omniscient through his ravens who inform him about everything, whereas God is omniscient by his own ability. But later Ariel says that God's many Angels keep him informed about people. I just find it confusing: what exactly is the definition of omniscient then? Is it just facts about the world as it is? Odin's ability to see the future is not addressed. The fact that God doesn't know how his creations would turn out, meaning that he doesn't know the future, does not diminish his ability to be omniscient. <br />That being said, is Odin omniscient or is he not? It's just an example, but I think there were things in this book that weren't defined well enough.<br /><br />- Ariel, as an entity without a body of flesh and blood, is able to a.o. move through walls. How is this still possible when he has Cecilie in his arms? Just being in Ariel's arms doesn't change the structure of Cecilie's body, and she should not be able to move through walls. This is not addressed or explained in the slightest.<br /><br />- Ariel mentions in the beginning that there's not enough Angels to watch over ill people. But there's also far more Angels than humans - because who else can enjoy this universe? Certainly not humans, because they are bound to planet Earth, and Angels are not. Why can't there be more Angels looking after people then? The reason certainly isn't that there aren't enough Angels... so why?<br /><br />- Speaking of Angels visiting the ill: sometimes they show themselves, but generally they don't. We never found out why Ariel decided to show himself to Cecilie, other than curiosity. But that doesn't explain why he chose her specifically, or why she was special. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I might remember things a tad wrongly, as I did read this on the train and that's not generally the best place to read very attentively. But these things just strike me as odd, add to that the almost absent characterization and a wafer-thin plot, and I just didn't enjoy this book as much as I could have.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11739049829231238101" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_820990524" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/820990524" />
    <a title="Ellen-Arwen Tristram" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7783445-ellen-arwen-tristram"><img alt="Ellen-Arwen Tristram" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1453403132p2/7783445.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/820990524?book_show_action=true">Jan 12, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ellen-Arwen Tristram" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ellen-Arwen Tristram" href="/user/show/7783445-ellen-arwen-tristram">Ellen-Arwen Tristram</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7783445-ellen-arwen-tristram?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7783445-ellen-arwen-tristram?shelf=reread">reread</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer820990524" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer612194286885118410">I reread this as a sort of warm-up to embarking on Sophie's World, which I have meant to read for rather a lot of years! I first read this when I was about eight or nine and I remember the huge impact it had on me then.<br/><br/>It's a compact, dense little book - although it is aimed at younger readers, there's a lot contained within the pages. It tells the story of Cecilia (or Cecille, in some translations, I believe) who is terminally ill and visited by an angel, Ariel. Basically, they philosophise abo</span>
  <span id="freeText612194286885118410" style="display:none">I reread this as a sort of warm-up to embarking on Sophie's World, which I have meant to read for rather a lot of years! I first read this when I was about eight or nine and I remember the huge impact it had on me then.<br /><br />It's a compact, dense little book - although it is aimed at younger readers, there's a lot contained within the pages. It tells the story of Cecilia (or Cecille, in some translations, I believe) who is terminally ill and visited by an angel, Ariel. Basically, they philosophise about the existence of God, what it means to be alive, what angels are, what feelings and sensations are, and what death means.<br /><br />I have never read another novel like it. Cecilia's shifting moods seem so realistic to me - the refusal to accept that she is dying, anger and bitterness at the world and at God for making things fade and perish, for the imperfections that make up life, and misplaced faith that she will recover to play in that winter's snow.<br /><br />Gaarder makes you think, but it is quite gentle, being a children's story. Anyone should read this; the religious aspects were fine with me (an atheist) and the experience of death is universal. I think it should be on the curriculum at schools!<br /><br />Although ultimately a sad ending, the book is still a joy to read. You almost forget whilst reading it that Cecilia is going to die, almost start believing her that she will get out to use her new skis. But by the end, she is accepting and sees her own head on the pillow from outside, looking from the other side of Ariel's looking glass. She is ready to leave.</span>
  <a data-text-id="612194286885118410" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1946077073" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1946077073" />
    <a title="Aaron Jesko" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38872336-aaron-jesko"><img alt="Aaron Jesko" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1489932169p2/38872336.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1946077073?book_show_action=true">Mar 19, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aaron Jesko" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aaron Jesko" href="/user/show/38872336-aaron-jesko">Aaron Jesko</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1946077073" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16998967610290873807">This little book does give food for thought. It’s a book for young readers and adults alike. And it’s for those who like the quiet stories. <br/><br/>In the story a young sick girl gets visited by an angel. They discuss heaven and earth, God and creation. It’s clear from the beginning, the girl is preparing for her departure from the physical realm. The angel is here to help her come to terms with her situation. <br/><br/>The story is a sweet idea and the questions discussed run deep, no doubt about that. But someh</span>
  <span id="freeText16998967610290873807" style="display:none">This little book does give food for thought. It’s a book for young readers and adults alike. And it’s for those who like the quiet stories. <br /><br />In the story a young sick girl gets visited by an angel. They discuss heaven and earth, God and creation. It’s clear from the beginning, the girl is preparing for her departure from the physical realm. The angel is here to help her come to terms with her situation. <br /><br />The story is a sweet idea and the questions discussed run deep, no doubt about that. But somehow I expected more from this book. <br />Let me tell you why. <br />For one the girl seems very together. Her character is just a little too constructed, too rational for my taste. The author surely wrote her that way for the sake of the discussion about philosophical and spiritual matters. But I think the story would have worked just as well if she had been a little less intellectual and more human/emotional. <br /><br />Also, I feel the girl accepts her situation far too easily. I can see something resembling the five stages of grief. But I believe it would have given the story even more depth if her struggle to come to terms with her fate had been more dramatic. This would have given even more weight to what the angel has to teach her. We learn best through contrast.<br /><br />In summary: the story is a sweet idea but doesn’t hit all the marks and not always the right tone. Although the questions discussed do give plenty of food for thought.<br /><br />I give three stars. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16998967610290873807" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1117142161" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1117142161" />
    <a title="Eleanor Toland" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12262345-eleanor-toland"><img alt="Eleanor Toland" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1413624851p2/12262345.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1117142161?book_show_action=true">Nov 27, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eleanor Toland" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eleanor Toland" href="/user/show/12262345-eleanor-toland">Eleanor Toland</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12262345-eleanor-toland?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12262345-eleanor-toland?shelf=kindertotenlieder">kindertotenlieder</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12262345-eleanor-toland?shelf=theological">theological</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12262345-eleanor-toland?shelf=angels">angels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12262345-eleanor-toland?shelf=christmas">christmas</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1117142161" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8084026360276871557">A slender book telling a deceptively simple story: the conversations between a terminally ill young girl and the angel who appears to comfort her as she lies bedridden and dying in the days before Christmas. Considering the subject matter, the writing is remarkably unsentimental. Cecelia and her guardian angel Ariel are complex, real characters. Cecelia's alternate states of denial, bitterness and calm resignation towards her fate are heart-rendingly convincing, and Ariel is one of the most orig</span>
  <span id="freeText8084026360276871557" style="display:none">A slender book telling a deceptively simple story: the conversations between a terminally ill young girl and the angel who appears to comfort her as she lies bedridden and dying in the days before Christmas. Considering the subject matter, the writing is remarkably unsentimental. Cecelia and her guardian angel Ariel are complex, real characters. Cecelia's alternate states of denial, bitterness and calm resignation towards her fate are heart-rendingly convincing, and Ariel is one of the most original and vividly inhuman angels I have come across in fiction. There is very little of a conventional plot here: the book is largely a series of dialogues interspersed with scenes of Cecelia's family preparing for the inevitable. But it works, and in my opinion works as a mix of philosophy and fiction far better than the more well-known <i>Sophie's World</i> by the same author. <br /> <br />Jostein Gaarder is unapologetically a Christian author: angels, Christmas and a retelling of the Garden of Eden feature. However, the religious aspects of the story are neither didactic or full of unconvincingly too-easy consolations. <i>Through a Glass, Darkly</i> is a memorable philosophical engagement with what is perhaps the greatest mystery of the human condition: death. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8084026360276871557" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1844655160?book_show_action=true">Jan 03, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hanna-Dora" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hanna-Dora" href="/user/show/34918967-hanna-dora">Hanna-Dora</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780753806739" href="/book/show/175831.Through_A_Glass_Darkly">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34918967-hanna-dora?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1844655160" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10908807631428286870">Jostein Gaarder is one of my favourite authors and I admire him deeply for bringing philosophy closer to children and writing young adult books that deal with so many difficult and profound ideas. This book of his is no exception, although I have to admit it was a bit too religious for my taste. I consider myself a religious person, but regardless of that, I think the book should have been more open about its ideas of the afterlife, more mysterious and vague. Apart from that, the story itself - </span>
  <span id="freeText10908807631428286870" style="display:none">Jostein Gaarder is one of my favourite authors and I admire him deeply for bringing philosophy closer to children and writing young adult books that deal with so many difficult and profound ideas. This book of his is no exception, although I have to admit it was a bit too religious for my taste. I consider myself a religious person, but regardless of that, I think the book should have been more open about its ideas of the afterlife, more mysterious and vague. Apart from that, the story itself - as usual by Gaarder - is brilliant, and it left me crying my eyes out in the end. I've recently lost my father to cancer and reading a story from a cancer patient's point of view was difficult but also, in a way, stangely comforting.<br />I loved the way how Gaarder <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[implied that Ariel was only a figment of Cecilia's imagination. I read the story that way from the start, but all the narrative solutions to make the story a mix or reality and imagination were really clever. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> It is a lovely, sad, and deep book with tons of wonderful ideas. Still, toning down all the religious talk a bit could have improved it quite a lot.<br /><i>The Orange Girl</i> is still my favourite book from Gaarder, but I enjoyed this story. The ending is incredibly moving and masterfully written.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10908807631428286870" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Felicity Terry" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Felicity Terry" href="/user/show/7331397-felicity-terry">Felicity Terry</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer464532509" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14861442168120720869">With an almost child-like, old-fashioned simplicity, Through A Glass Darkly is beautifully spiritual, philosophical, insightful and sentimental and yet never mushy.<br/><br/>The story of a young terminally ill girl (Cecilia) who, one Christmas, is befriended by an angel (Arial) the story is complex in so far as it takes a look at what it is to be human whist at the same time exploring life after death which though never overtly 'preachy' is told from a fairly religious point on view that might not appeal </span>
  <span id="freeText14861442168120720869" style="display:none">With an almost child-like, old-fashioned simplicity, Through A Glass Darkly is beautifully spiritual, philosophical, insightful and sentimental and yet never mushy.<br /><br />The story of a young terminally ill girl (Cecilia) who, one Christmas, is befriended by an angel (Arial) the story is complex in so far as it takes a look at what it is to be human whist at the same time exploring life after death which though never overtly 'preachy' is told from a fairly religious point on view that might not appeal to everyone.<br /><br />The sign of a good writer that they can awaken so many emotions, provoke so many reactions, I thought the author did a particularly good job with Cecilia in that on the one hand (despite/because of her illness?) I found her to be a bit of an unlikeable spoilt brat and yet on the other I felt so much compassion for her and not just because of her illness.<br /><br />A great read for older children/teenagers, as an adult reading this I felt that some of the issues could have been explored more thoroughly, this is never the less a wonderfully thought provoking, in many ways, life affirming novel.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14861442168120720869" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14603123653022404684">Okay, I’ll come clean, I have never actually read Jostein Gaarder’s Sophie’s World. I know everyone always recommends it, it’s always on every book list I ever come across and, to make matters worse, I even have my own copy that I bought from the Penrith Library. I just never managed to get the whole way through it, I will try again … but not today. Anyways, when I saw this book sitting next to it on the shelf at the library I decided to give this, decidedly smaller (and much more manageable) on</span>
  <span id="freeText14603123653022404684" style="display:none">Okay, I’ll come clean, I have never actually read Jostein Gaarder’s Sophie’s World. I know everyone always recommends it, it’s always on every book list I ever come across and, to make matters worse, I even have my own copy that I bought from the Penrith Library. I just never managed to get the whole way through it, I will try again … but not today. Anyways, when I saw this book sitting next to it on the shelf at the library I decided to give this, decidedly smaller (and much more manageable) one a read.<br /><br />It is the story of a girl who (though it is never said explicitly) knows she is dying of cancer and is spending her last days at home with her family. One night she wakes to see a small white figure sitting on her windowsill watching her: an angel. The pair make a deal, she will tell him what it means to be human, if he will tell her what it is like to be an angel. Very beautiful, very sad, and, unsurprisingly for Gaardner, steeped in philosophy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14603123653022404684" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

Well, if I have a kid one day, Im gonna ask them to read this when they are still kids.</span>

<div id="review_522506276" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/522506276" />
    <a title="heidi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8320288-heidi"><img alt="heidi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546762967p2/8320288.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/522506276?book_show_action=true">Jan 31, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="heidi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="heidi" href="/user/show/8320288-heidi">heidi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer522506276" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15722817185162175731">A weird reading experience from Jostein Gaarder, and not in a good way. I mean, Gaarder specializes in weird. He is good at placing an engaging character (usually teenagers or young adults) in weird circumstances that causes them to question their existence. This book does the same, but I didn't want to care about Cecilia and her fate. The dialogues between Cecilia and the angel Ariel did nothing for me either.<br/><br/>I'm not sure if the charm of Gaarder's prose had been lost in translation, or if the C</span>
  <span id="freeText15722817185162175731" style="display:none">A weird reading experience from Jostein Gaarder, and not in a good way. I mean, Gaarder specializes in weird. He is good at placing an engaging character (usually teenagers or young adults) in weird circumstances that causes them to question their existence. This book does the same, but I didn't want to care about Cecilia and her fate. The dialogues between Cecilia and the angel Ariel did nothing for me either.<br /><br />I'm not sure if the charm of Gaarder's prose had been lost in translation, or if the Christian tone of the dialogues was the one that spoiled it for me. Having read Sophie's World and Solitaire Mystery, I had the impression that Gaarder is more philosophical than religious. Therefore coming across overtly Christian explanations for our existence in the universe (and traditional biblical ones, too, straight out of Creationist school) was unsettling and disappointing for me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15722817185162175731" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1604363200" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1604363200" />
    <a title="Inez" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11586785-inez"><img alt="Inez" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1480385433p2/11586785.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1604363200?book_show_action=true">Apr 08, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Inez" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Inez" href="/user/show/11586785-inez">Inez</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1604363200" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17474966736607459363">As the Indonesian edition for this book is titled "Dunia Sesilia" and mentioned as the sequel of Sophie's World, I kinda hoped that it was as complicated as Sophie. It turned out much simple--yet still philosophical.<br/><br/>And like any other "what if" stories, this novel made me questioning some of the things happening in this world--especially about the relationship between human and God. Although Gaarder used Christian point of view in this book, I still got the message.<br/><br/>Unfortunately, the plot's quit</span>
  <span id="freeText17474966736607459363" style="display:none">As the Indonesian edition for this book is titled "Dunia Sesilia" and mentioned as the sequel of Sophie's World, I kinda hoped that it was as complicated as Sophie. It turned out much simple--yet still philosophical.<br /><br />And like any other "what if" stories, this novel made me questioning some of the things happening in this world--especially about the relationship between human and God. Although Gaarder used Christian point of view in this book, I still got the message.<br /><br />Unfortunately, the plot's quite monotone. It reminded me of Paulo Coelho's novel "By the River Piedra, I Sat Down and Wept", but less adventurous. So it felt a bit flat. But as usual, Gaarder can create words worth to quote.<br /><br />You can put it on your wish-to-read list, but take it for a reading material while waiting for the next train.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17474966736607459363" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Elaine Oliveira" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4382933-elaine-oliveira"><img alt="Elaine Oliveira" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1491878045p2/4382933.jpg" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/125908631?book_show_action=true">Oct 12, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elaine Oliveira" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elaine Oliveira" href="/user/show/4382933-elaine-oliveira">Elaine Oliveira</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer125908631" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5493029875058326651">It's by Gaarder, it's philosophical.<br/><br/>This is Cecilie’s story. She’s a young girl who was faced with terminal cancer. We meet Cecilie at Christmas time, when her time on Earth is about to end, and follow her secret meetings with Ariel, an angel with sapphire-coloured eyes that comes to guide her to the other side.<br/><br/>It’s a short book, and once again Gaarder raises questions for us to ponder about. Hopefully, we'll all have improved ourselves a little by the end of it. Or, in the least, we'll be willi</span>
  <span id="freeText5493029875058326651" style="display:none">It's by Gaarder, it's philosophical.<br /><br />This is Cecilie’s story. She’s a young girl who was faced with terminal cancer. We meet Cecilie at Christmas time, when her time on Earth is about to end, and follow her secret meetings with Ariel, an angel with sapphire-coloured eyes that comes to guide her to the other side.<br /><br />It’s a short book, and once again Gaarder raises questions for us to ponder about. Hopefully, we'll all have improved ourselves a little by the end of it. Or, in the least, we'll be willing to try it.<br /><br />It’s so deep and so well written that I barely noticed I was reading a tragic tale. Or maybe that's because it can’t be deemed tragic when you see through the lens Gaarder gave us here.<br /><br />I’d recommend it to everyone. We'll all eventually face the same troubles as Cecilie.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5493029875058326651" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

To be honest, not my favourite of Gaarder's books so far. Interesting, but nothing new for him, and the god-religious aspect did get a bit repetitive. Distracting her from death and dying, or making her come to terms with it - something like that. </span>

<div id="review_190836330" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/190836330" />
    <a title="Emma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5898930-emma"><img alt="Emma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1379156742p2/5898930.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/190836330?book_show_action=true">Jul 27, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma" href="/user/show/5898930-emma">Emma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780753806739" href="/book/show/175831.Through_A_Glass_Darkly">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer190836330" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3959458707227276307">Gaarder has an amazing talent for making the vagueries of Philosophy into the wonders of the world. While not as in depth as his more famous works, 'Sophie's World' and 'The Solitare Mystery' this shorter work stil contains some beautifully simple thoughts on the ways of the world, simple because they should be obvious but they're not. However, I struggled to sympathise with Cecilia's character and didn't like her as much as his child protagonists in other novels. Definitely worth reading for fa</span>
  <span id="freeText3959458707227276307" style="display:none">Gaarder has an amazing talent for making the vagueries of Philosophy into the wonders of the world. While not as in depth as his more famous works, 'Sophie's World' and 'The Solitare Mystery' this shorter work stil contains some beautifully simple thoughts on the ways of the world, simple because they should be obvious but they're not. However, I struggled to sympathise with Cecilia's character and didn't like her as much as his child protagonists in other novels. Definitely worth reading for fans of Gaarder's but if you're new to his works I'd recommend starting with one of his more famous books as they display his talent for making philosophy engaging for all much better.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3959458707227276307" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/543996729" />

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer543996729" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5851625464151197359">I do like Gaarder's book, but this one seems more like the bare skeleton of a structure he was laying for his other books. Several of these ideas are presented much better in the Orange Girl, Solitaire Mystery, and Sophie's world. In comparison, this books comes off as childlish and half-baked. It also loses points for stating some factually incorrect theories, such as the myth that we only use 10 per cent of our brains.<br/><br/>I regret to say that this books must be dismissed as a silly little collecti</span>
  <span id="freeText5851625464151197359" style="display:none">I do like Gaarder's book, but this one seems more like the bare skeleton of a structure he was laying for his other books. Several of these ideas are presented much better in the Orange Girl, Solitaire Mystery, and Sophie's world. In comparison, this books comes off as childlish and half-baked. It also loses points for stating some factually incorrect theories, such as the myth that we only use 10 per cent of our brains.<br /><br />I regret to say that this books must be dismissed as a silly little collection of pseudointellectual conversations between a delirious girl and an "angel". If you want to try out Gaarder's books, Orange Girl and Solitaire mystery are much better choices.</span>

<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('2Jl1+bZnj+bY3uUR31FiFmrC9N8T/VBrsnZvaCYvPrLx5uvwIwWWYcC4pluE57LDinM+AgKketAhqn9UwXEnmw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('RG+9kW6dkUqefdHQlftT0SSZ0VCLlSr417fxpXrqYlNtECOY+/+IzYYbkprOTYMExCgbjZrMAENEa+GZnbR7eg==')})
  }
//]]>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/1388082.Jostein_Gaarder">About Jostein Gaarder</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/1388082.Jostein_Gaarder"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1546539876p3/1388082.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>

</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
5,835
followers

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer5199461568567696921">Jostein Gaarder is a Norwegian intellectual and author of several novels, short stories, and children's books. Gaarder often writes from the perspective of children, exploring their sense of wonder about the world. He often uses meta-fiction in his works, writing stories within stories.<br/><br/>Gaarder was born into a pedagogical family. His best known work is the novel <i>Sophie's World</i>, subtitled "A Novel a</span>
  <span id="freeText5199461568567696921" style="display:none">Jostein Gaarder is a Norwegian intellectual and author of several novels, short stories, and children's books. Gaarder often writes from the perspective of children, exploring their sense of wonder about the world. He often uses meta-fiction in his works, writing stories within stories.<br /><br />Gaarder was born into a pedagogical family. His best known work is the novel <i>Sophie's World</i>, subtitled "A Novel about the History of Philosophy." This popular work has been translated into fifty-three languages; there are over thirty million copies in print, with three million copies sold in Germany alone.<br /><br />In 1997, he established the Sophie Prize together with his wife Siri Dannevig. This prize is an international environment and development prize (USD 100,000 = 77,000 €), awarded annually. It is named after the novel.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5199461568567696921" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
